black;">900</td></tr></table><h6>Unordered Tetrad Three Gene Mapping</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes A and B is [AB] cM (AB)</li><li>The distance between genes A and C is [AC] cM (AC)</li><li>The distance between genes B and C is [BC] cM (BC)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	AB	5		AC	22		BC	19		geneorder	abc	cba

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes J and K is [JK] cM (JK)</li><li>The distance between genes J and L is [JL] cM (JL)</li><li>The distance between genes K and L is [KL] cM (KL)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	JK	5		JL	16		KL	12		geneorder	jkl	lkj

Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes N and P is [NP] cM (NP)</li><li>The distance between genes N and Q is [NQ] cM (NQ)</li><li>The distance between genes P and Q is [PQ] cM (PQ)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes U and V is [UV] cM (UV)</li><li>The distance between genes U and W is [UW] cM (UW)</li><li>The distance between genes V and W is [VW] cM (VW)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	UV	27		UW	9		VW	19		geneorder	uwv	vwu

black;">2400</td></tr></table><h6>Unordered Tetrad Three Gene Mapping</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes F and G is [FG] cM (FG)</li><li>The distance between genes F and H is [FH] cM (FH)</li><li>The distance between genes G and H is [GH] cM (GH)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	FG	28		FH	11		GH	18		geneorder	fhg	ghf

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes P and Q is [PQ] cM (PQ)</li><li>The distance between genes P and R is [PR] cM (PR)</li><li>The distance between genes Q and R is [QR] cM (QR)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	PQ	13		PR	7		QR	18		geneorder	qpr	rpq

Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes F and G is [FG] cM (FG)</li><li>The distance between genes F and H is [FH] cM (FH)</li><li>The distance between genes G and H is [GH] cM (GH)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	FG	19		FH	28		GH	10		geneorder	fgh	hgf

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes P and Q is [PQ] cM (PQ)</li><li>The distance between genes P and R is [PR] cM (PR)</li><li>The distance between genes Q and R is [QR] cM (QR)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	PQ	7		PR	13		QR	18		geneorder	qpr	rpq

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes B and C is [BC] cM (BC)</li><li>The distance between genes B and D is [BD] cM (BD)</li><li>The distance between genes C and D is [CD] cM (CD)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	BC	22		BD	15		CD	8		geneorder	bdc	cdb

Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes K and L is [KL] cM (KL)</li><li>The distance between genes K and M is [KM] cM (KM)</li><li>The distance between genes L and M is [LM] cM (LM)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	KL	21		KM	9		LM	27		geneorder	lkm	mkl

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes V and W is [VW] cM (VW)</li><li>The distance between genes V and X is [VX] cM (VX)</li><li>The distance between genes W and X is [WX] cM (WX)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	VW	20		VX	11		WX	30		geneorder	wvx	xvw

black;">1200</td></tr></table><h6>Unordered Tetrad Three Gene Mapping</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among three genes. <p>Using the table, determine the order of the genes and the distances between them. Once calculated, fill in the following four blanks: </p><ul><li>The distance between genes G and H is [GH] cM (GH)</li><li>The distance between genes G and I is [GI] cM (GI)</li><li>The distance between genes H and I is [HI] cM (HI)</li><li>From this the correct order of the genes is [geneorder] (gene order).</li></ul><p><i>Hint 1:</i> ALL gene distances will be whole numbers,  do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are wrong.</p><p><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only letters or numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Type for all three genes.</li><li>Step 2: Pick any two genes and assign PD, NPD, TT</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul><li>Step 5: Go to Step 2 and pick a new pair of genes until all pairs are complete.</li></ul>	GH	11		GI	26		HI	16		geneorder	ghi	ihg
